There\\n11: /// is no \\\"pass\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\n18: /// single module provided.\\n19: ///\\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\\n21: /// modules and functions.\\n22: ///\\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\\n24: ///   a Function.\\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\\n26: ///\\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \\\"Value Semantics and Concept-based\\n29: /// Polymorphism\\\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \\\"Inheritance Is The Base\\n30: /// Class of Evil\\\") by Sean Parent:\\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\\n34: ///\\n35: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n36: \\n37: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n38: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n39: \\n40: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\\\"\\n41: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\\\"\\n42: #include <list>\\n52: #include <memory>\\n53: #include <tuple>\\n54: #include <type_traits>\\n55: #include <utility>\\n56: #include <vector>\\n57: \\n58: namespace llvm {\\n59: \\n60: class Function;\\n61: class Module;\\n62: \\n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\\n65: \\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\n67: /// passes.\\n68: ///\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n74:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\"llvm::\\\");\\n77:     return Name;\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\n84:     OS << PassName;\\n85:   }\\n86: };\\n87: \\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\n89: ///\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n111:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\\n113:   }\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: namespace detail {\\n117: \\n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n121:           typename... ArgTs, size_t... Ns>\\n122: typename PassT::Result\\n123: getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\\n124:                              std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\\n125:                              std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\\n126:   (void)Args;\\n127:   return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: /// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\\n131: ///\\n132: /// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\\n133: /// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\\n134: /// pass to getResult.\\n135: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... AnalysisArgTs,\\n136:           typename... MainArgTs>\\n137: typename PassT::Result\\n138: getAnalysisResult(AnalysisManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisArgTs...> &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\\n139:                   std::tuple<MainArgTs...> Args) {\\n140:   return (getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple<\\n141:           PassT, IRUnitT>)(AM, IR, Args,\\n142:                            std::index_sequence_for<AnalysisArgTs...>{});\\n143: }\\n144: \\n145: } // namespace detail\\n146: \\n147: /// Manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR.\\n148: ///\\n149: /// A pass manager contains a sequence of passes to run over a particular unit\\n150: /// of IR (e.g. Functions, Modules). It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\\n171:   // duplicated code here.\\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\\n173: \\n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\\n176:     return *this;\\n177:   }\\n178: \\n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\\\",\\\");\\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\\n183:       OS << LS;\\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\\n185:     }\\n186:   }\\n187: \\n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h%3FL1-200\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b18a42d1-4920-4e2a-aad4-382806870c0a","uuid":"2fa26b90-09a8-47e6-87d1-0ab14855a879","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: //===- PassManager.h - Pass management infrastructure -----------*- C++ -*-===//\\n2: //\\n3: // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\\n4: // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\\n5: // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\\n6: //\\n7: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n8: /// \\\\file\\n9: ///\\n10: /// This header defines various interfaces for pass management in LLVM. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n111:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\\n113:   }\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: namespace detail {\\n117: \\n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n121:           typename... Ns>\\n122: typename PassT::Result\\n123: getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\\n124:                              std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\\n125:                              std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\\n126:   (void)Args;\\n127:   return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: /// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\\n131: ///\\n132: /// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\\n133: /// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\\n134: /// pass to getResult.\\n135: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h%3FL1-200\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: //===- PassManager.h - Pass management infrastructure -----------*- C++ -*-===//\n2: //\n3: // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n4: // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n5: // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n6: //\n7: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n8: /// \\file\n9: ///\n10: /// This header defines various interfaces for pass management in LLVM. There\n11: /// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n18: /// single module provided.\n19: ///\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n21: /// modules and functions.\n22: ///\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n24: ///   a Function.\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n26: ///\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n29: /// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n30: /// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\n34: ///\n35: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n36: \n37: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n38: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n39: \n40: #include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n41: #include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n42: #include \"llvm/ADT/StringExtras.h\"\n43: #include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n44: #include \"llvm/ADT/TinyPtrVector.h\"\n45: #include \"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\"\n46: #include \"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\"\n47: #include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n48: #include \"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\"\n49: #include <cassert>\n50: #include <cstring>\n51: #include <list>\n52: #include <memory>\n53: #include <tuple>\n54: #include <type_traits>\n55: #include <utility>\n56: #include <vector>\n57: \n58: namespace llvm {\n59: \n60: class Function;\n61: class Module;\n62: \n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... Doing this could\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\n209:   template <typename PassT>\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\n214:   }\n215: \n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\n218: \n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\n220: \n221: protected:\n222:   using PassConceptT =\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\n224: \n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\n226: };\n227: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h%3FL158-226"}}}

This template is used in the follow manner (at global scope, in\\n83: /// your .cpp file):\\n84: ///\\n85: /// static RegisterPass<YourPassClassName> tmp(\\\"passopt\\\", \\\"My Pass Name\\\");\\n86: ///\\n87: /// This statement will cause your pass to be created by calling the default\\n88: /// constructor exposed by the pass.\\n89: template <typename passName> struct RegisterPass : public PassInfo {\\n90:   // Register Pass using default constructor...\\n91:   RegisterPass(StringRef PassArg, StringRef Name, bool CFGOnly = false,\\n92:                bool is_analysis = false)\\n93:       : PassInfo(Name, PassArg, &passName::ID,\\n94:                  PassInfo::NormalCtor_t(callDefaultCtor<passName>), CFGOnly,\\n95:                  is_analysis) {\\n96:     PassRegistry::getPassRegistry()->registerPass(*this);\\n97:   }\\n98: };\\n99: \\n100: //===---------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n101: /// PassRegistrationListener class - This class is meant to be derived from by\\n102: /// clients that are interested in which passes get registered and unregistered\\n103: /// at runtime (which can be because of the RegisterPass constructors being run\\n104: /// as the program starts up, or may be because a shared object just got\\n105: /// loaded).\\n106: struct PassRegistrationListener {\\n107:   PassRegistrationListener() = default;\\n108:   virtual ~PassRegistrationListener() = default;\\n109: \\n110:   /// Callback functions - // This is still a valid proxy.\\n38: \\n39:   // If this proxy isn't marked as preserved, then even if the result remains\\n40:   // valid, the key itself may no longer be valid, so we clear everything.\\n41:   //\\n42:   // Note that in order to preserve this proxy, a module pass must ensure that\\n43:   // the FAM has been completely updated to handle the deletion of functions.\\n44:   // Specifically, any FAM-cached results for those functions need to have been\\n45:   // forcibly cleared. When preserved, this proxy will only invalidate results\\n46:   // cached on functions *still in the module* at the end of the module pass.\\n47:   auto PAC = PA.getChecker<FunctionAnalysisManagerModuleProxy>();\\n48:   if (!PAC.preserved() && !PAC.preservedSet<AllAnalysesOn<Module>>()) {\\n49:     InnerAM->clear();\\n50:     return true;\\n51:   }\\n52: \\n53:   // Directly check if the relevant set is preserved.\\n54:   bool AreFunctionAnalysesPreserved =\\n55:       PA.allAnalysesInSetPreserved<AllAnalysesOn<Function>>();\\n56: \\n57:   // Now walk all the functions to see if any inner analysis invalidation is\\n58:   // necessary.\\n59:   for (Function &F : M) {\\n60:     std::optional<PreservedAnalyses> FunctionPA;\\n61: \\n62:     // Check to see whether the preserved set needs to be pruned based on\\n63:     // module-level analysis invalidation that triggers deferred invalidation\\n64:     // registered with the outer analysis manager proxy for this function.\\n65:     if (auto *OuterProxy =\\n66:             InnerAM->getCachedResult<ModuleAnalysisManagerFunctionProxy>(F))\\n67:       for (const auto &OuterInvalidationPair :\\n68:            OuterProxy->getOuterInvalidations()) {\\n69:         AnalysisKey *OuterAnalysisID = OuterInvalidationPair.first;\\n70:         const auto &InnerAnalysisIDs = OuterInvalidationPair.second;\\n71:         if (Inv.invalidate(OuterAnalysisID, M, PA)) {\\n72:           if (!FunctionPA)\\n73:             FunctionPA = PA;\\n74:           for (AnalysisKey
